\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{AutoThreshold()}{AutoThreshold()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static void Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Auto\+Threshold (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}}}]{b,  }\item[{bool}]{update\+Image\+Stats }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

It takes a \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object, and calculates the mean histogram for each channel, and for the entire image.

The \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object is a class that contains a list of buffers, each of which contains a byte array of pixel data.

The function also calculates the mean histogram for each buffer, and stores it in the buffer\textquotesingle{}s stats property.

The function also calculates the mean histogram for each channel, and stores it in the channel\textquotesingle{}s stats property.

The function also calculates the mean histogram for the entire image, and stores it in the image\textquotesingle{}s statistics property.

The mean histogram is calculated by adding up the histograms of each buffer, and then dividing by the number of buffers.

The histogram is calculated by looping through the byte array of pixel data, and incrementing the value of the histogram at the index of the pixel value.

The histogram

{\em update\+Image\+Stats} & if true, the image stats will be updated. \\

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ExtractRegionFromTiledTiff()}{ExtractRegionFromTiledTiff()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static Bitmap Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Extract\+Region\+From\+Tiled\+Tiff (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}}}]{b,  }\item[{int}]{x,  }\item[{int}]{y,  }\item[{int}]{width,  }\item[{int}]{height,  }\item[{int}]{res }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

The function Extract\+Region\+From\+Tiled\+Tiff takes a \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object, coordinates, width, height, and resolution as input, and returns a Bitmap object representing the extracted region from the tiled TIFF image.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}}} & The \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object represents an image file that contains multiple pages or resolutions. It contains information about the image file, such as the file path, the number of pages, and the format of each page. \\
\hline
{\em x} & The x-\/coordinate of the top-\/left corner of the region to extract from the tiled TIFF image. \\
\hline
{\em y} & The parameter \char`\"{}y\char`\"{} represents the starting y-\/coordinate of the region to be extracted from the tiled TIFF image. \\
\hline
{\em width} & The width parameter represents the width of the region to be extracted from the tiled TIFF image. \\
\hline
{\em height} & The height parameter represents the height of the region to be extracted from the tiled TIFF image. \\
\hline
{\em res} & The parameter \char`\"{}res\char`\"{} represents the resolution level of the tiled TIFF image. It is used to specify the level of detail or zoom level at which the image is being extracted.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The method is returning a Bitmap object. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image_a57ac54ac7ebe4e1cabad20073ec05e78}\label{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image_a57ac54ac7ebe4e1cabad20073ec05e78}} 
\index{BioImager.BioImage@{BioImager.BioImage}!FilesToStack@{FilesToStack}}
\index{FilesToStack@{FilesToStack}!BioImager.BioImage@{BioImager.BioImage}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{FilesToStack()}{FilesToStack()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Files\+To\+Stack (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{string\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{files,  }\item[{int}]{sizeZ,  }\item[{int}]{sizeC,  }\item[{int}]{sizeT }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

It takes a list of files, and creates a new \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object with the first file in the list. Then it loops through the rest of the files, adding the buffers from each file to the new \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object. Finally, it updates the coordinates of the new \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object, and adds it to the Images list


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em files} & an array of file paths \\
\hline
{\em sizeZ} & number of slices in the stack \\
\hline
{\em sizeC} & number of channels \\
\hline
{\em sizeT} & number of time points\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily static int Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Find\+Focus (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}}}]{im,  }\item[{int}]{Channel,  }\item[{int}]{Time }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

The function finds the focus of a given \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} at a specific channel and time by calculating the focus quality of each Z-\/plane and returning the coordinate with the highest focus quality.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}}} & A \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object that contains the image data. \\

{\em Channel} & The channel of the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} to analyze. A \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} can have multiple channels, each representing a different fluorescent label or imaging modality. \\
\hline
{\em Time} & The time point at which the focus is being calculated.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an integer value which represents the coordinate of the image with the highest focus quality in a given channel and time. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{GetBitsPerPixel()}{GetBitsPerPixel()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static int Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Get\+Bits\+Per\+Pixel (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{bt }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

\begin{quote}
If the number is less than or equal to 255, then it\textquotesingle{}s 8 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal \end{quote}
to 512, then it\textquotesingle{}s 9 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal to 1023, then it\textquotesingle{}s 10 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal to 2047, then it\textquotesingle{}s 11 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal to 4095, then it\textquotesingle{}s 12 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal to 8191, then it\textquotesingle{}s 13 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal to 16383, then it\textquotesingle{}s 14 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal to 32767, then it\textquotesingle{}s 15 bits. If it\textquotesingle{}s less than or equal to 65535, then it\textquotesingle{}s 16 bits


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em bt} & The number of bits per pixel.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The number of bits per pixel. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily int Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Get\+Index (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{ix,  }\item[{int}]{iy }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{quote}
Get\+Index(x,y) = (y $\ast$ stridex + x) $\ast$ 2 \end{quote}
The stridex is the width of the image in bytes.

The stridey is the height of the image in bytes.

The stridex and stridey are the same for a square image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

The stridex and stridey are different for a rectangular image.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily static Pixel\+Format Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Get\+Pixel\+Format (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{rgb\+Channel\+Count,  }\item[{int}]{bits\+Per\+Pixel }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

If the bits per pixel is 8, then the pixel format is either 8bpp\+Indexed, 24bpp\+Rgb, or 32bpp\+Argb. If the bits per pixel is 16, then the pixel format is either 16bpp\+Gray\+Scale or 48bpp\+Rgb

{\em bits\+Per\+Pixel} & 8 or 16\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The Pixel\+Format of the image. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{OMESupport()}{OMESupport()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static bool Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+OMESupport (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

The function checks if the operating system is mac\+OS and displays a message if OME images are not supported, otherwise it sets Ome\+Support to true.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The method is returning a boolean value. If the operating system is Mac\+OS and the support\+Dialog flag is false, it will display a message dialog and return false. Otherwise, it will set the Ome\+Support flag to true and return true. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image_a7a27d4f9940f198f4038d4e52cf19725}\label{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image_a7a27d4f9940f198f4038d4e52cf19725}} 
\index{BioImager.BioImage@{BioImager.BioImage}!OpenFile@{OpenFile}}
\index{OpenFile@{OpenFile}!BioImager.BioImage@{BioImager.BioImage}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{OpenFile()}{OpenFile()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [4/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Open\+File (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{string}]{file,  }\item[{int}]{series,  }\item[{bool}]{tab,  }\item[{bool}]{add\+To\+Images,  }\item[{bool}]{tile,  }\item[{int}]{tileX,  }\item[{int}]{tileY,  }\item[{int}]{tile\+SizeX,  }\item[{int}]{tile\+SizeY }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

The Open\+File function in C\# opens a \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} file, reads its metadata, and loads the image data into a \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em file} & The file path of the bioimage to be opened. \\
\hline
{\em series} & The series parameter is an integer that specifies the series number of the image to open. \\
\hline
{\em tab} & The \char`\"{}tab\char`\"{} parameter is a boolean value that determines whether the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} should be opened in a new tab or not. If set to true, the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} will be opened in a new tab. If set to false, the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} will be opened in the current tab. \\
\hline
{\em add\+To\+Images} & A boolean value indicating whether the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} should be added to the Images collection. \\
\hline
{\em tile} & The \char`\"{}tile\char`\"{} parameter is a boolean value that determines whether the image should be opened as a tiled image or not. If set to true, the image will be opened as a tiled image. If set to false, the image will be opened as a regular image. \\
\hline
{\em tileX} & The {\ttfamily tileX} parameter is an integer that represents the starting X coordinate of the tile. It is used when opening a tiled image to specify the position of the tile within the image. \\
\hline
{\em tileY} & The {\ttfamily tileY} parameter is used to specify the starting Y coordinate of the tile when opening a tiled image. It determines the position of the tile within the image. \\
\hline
{\em tile\+SizeX} & The tile\+SizeX parameter is the width of each tile in pixels. It is used when opening a tiled TIFF image to specify the size of the tiles. \\
\hline
{\em tile\+SizeY} & The tile\+SizeY parameter is the height of each tile in pixels when the image is tiled.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The method is returning a \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} object. 
\end{DoxyReturn}


Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{_bio_8cs_source_l04782}{4782}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{_bio_8cs_source}{Bio.\+cs}}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily static \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Open\+OME (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{string}]{file,  }\item[{bool}]{tab }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

The function \char`\"{}\+Open\+OME\char`\"{} opens a bioimage file in the OME format and returns the first image in the series.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{OpenOME()}{OpenOME()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [3/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Open\+OME (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{string}]{file,  }\item[{int}]{serie,  }\item[{bool}]{tab,  }\item[{bool}]{add\+To\+Images,  }\item[{bool}]{tile,  }\item[{int}]{tilex,  }\item[{int}]{tiley,  }\item[{int}]{tile\+SizeX,  }\item[{int}]{tile\+SizeY,  }\item[{bool}]{use\+Open\+Slide = {\ttfamily true} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}



The function \char`\"{}\+Open\+OME\char`\"{} opens a bioimage file, with options to specify the series, whether to 

The function \char`\"{}\+Open\+OME\char`\"{} opens a bioimage file, with options to specify the series, whether to display it in a tab, whether to add it to existing images, whether to tile the image, and the tile size.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em file} & The file parameter is a string that represents the file path or name of the OME (Open Microscopy Environment) file that you want to open. \\
\hline
{\em serie} & The \char`\"{}serie\char`\"{} parameter is an integer that represents the series number of the image to be opened. \\
\hline
{\em tab} & The \char`\"{}tab\char`\"{} parameter is a boolean value that determines whether the image should be opened in a new tab or not. If set to true, the image will be opened in a new tab. If set to false, the image will be opened in the current tab. \\
\hline
{\em add\+To\+Images} & The \char`\"{}add\+To\+Images\char`\"{} parameter is a boolean value that determines whether the opened image should be added to a collection of images. If set to true, the image will be added to the collection. If set to false, the image will not be added. \\
\hline
{\em tile} & The \char`\"{}tile\char`\"{} parameter is a boolean value that determines whether or not to tile the images. If set to true, the images will be tiled according to the specified tilex, tiley, tile\+SizeX, and tile\+SizeY parameters. If set to false, the images will not be tiled. \\
\hline
{\em tilex} & The parameter \char`\"{}tilex\char`\"{} is an integer that represents the starting x-\/coordinate of the tile. \\
\hline
{\em tiley} & The parameter \char`\"{}tiley\char`\"{} is used to specify the number of tiles in the y-\/direction when tiling the image. \\
\hline
{\em tile\+SizeX} & The tile\+SizeX parameter specifies the width of each tile in pixels when tiling the images. \\
\hline
{\em tile\+SizeY} & The tile\+SizeY parameter is the height of each tile in pixels when tiling the images. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\DoxyCodeLine{06088                         \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (b.meta.getPixelsPhysicalSizeZ(r) != \textcolor{keyword}{null})}
\DoxyCodeLine{06089                         \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06090                             res.PhysicalSizeZ = b.meta.getPixelsPhysicalSizeZ(r).value().doubleValue();}
\DoxyCodeLine{06091                         \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06092                         \textcolor{keywordflow}{else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06093                         \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06094                             res.PhysicalSizeZ = 1;}
\DoxyCodeLine{06095                         \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06096                     \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06097                     \textcolor{keywordflow}{catch} (Exception e)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06098                     \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06099                         Console.WriteLine(\textcolor{stringliteral}{"{}No Stage Coordinates. PhysicalSize:("{}} + res.PhysicalSizeX + \textcolor{stringliteral}{"{},"{}} + res.PhysicalSizeY + \textcolor{stringliteral}{"{},"{}} + res.PhysicalSizeZ + \textcolor{stringliteral}{"{})"{}});}
\DoxyCodeLine{06100                     \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06101                     rss.Add(res);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06102                 \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06103             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06104             reader.setSeries(serie);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06105 }
\DoxyCodeLine{06106             \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} pyramidCount = 0;}
\DoxyCodeLine{06107             \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} pyramidResolutions = 0;}
\DoxyCodeLine{06108             List<Tuple<int, int>> prs = \textcolor{keyword}{new} List<Tuple<int, int>>();}
\DoxyCodeLine{06109             \textcolor{comment}{//We need to determine if this image is pyramidal or not.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06110             \textcolor{comment}{//We do this by seeing if the resolutions are downsampled or not.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06111             \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (rss.Count > 1 \&\& b.Type != ImageType.well)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06112             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06113                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (rss[0].SizeX > rss[1].SizeX)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06114                 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06115                     b.Type = ImageType.pyramidal;}
\DoxyCodeLine{06116                     tile = \textcolor{keyword}{true};}
\DoxyCodeLine{06117                     \textcolor{comment}{//We need to determine number of pyramids in this image and which belong to the series we are opening.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06118                     \textcolor{keywordtype}{int}? sr = \textcolor{keyword}{null};}
\DoxyCodeLine{06119                     \textcolor{keywordflow}{for} (\textcolor{keywordtype}{int} r = 0; r < rss.Count -\/ 1; r++)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06120                     \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06121                         \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (rss[r].SizeX > rss[r + 1].SizeX \&\& rss[r].PixelFormat == rss[r + 1].PixelFormat)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06122                         \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06123                             \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (sr == \textcolor{keyword}{null})}
\DoxyCodeLine{06124                             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06125                                 sr = r;}
\DoxyCodeLine{06126                                 prs.Add(\textcolor{keyword}{new} Tuple<int, int>(r, 0));}
\DoxyCodeLine{06127                             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06128                         \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06129                         \textcolor{keywordflow}{else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06130                         \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06131                             \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (rss[prs[prs.Count -\/ 1].Item1].PixelFormat == rss[r].PixelFormat)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06132                                 prs[prs.Count -\/ 1] = \textcolor{keyword}{new} Tuple<int, int>(prs[prs.Count -\/ 1].Item1, r);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06133                             sr = \textcolor{keyword}{null};}
\DoxyCodeLine{06134                         \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06135                     \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06136                     pyramidCount = prs.Count;}
\DoxyCodeLine{06137                     \textcolor{keywordflow}{for} (\textcolor{keywordtype}{int} p = 0; p < prs.Count; p++)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06138                     \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06139                         pyramidResolutions += (prs[p].Item2 -\/ prs[p].Item1) + 1;}
\DoxyCodeLine{06140                     \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06141 }
\DoxyCodeLine{06142                     \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (prs[serie].Item2 == 0)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06143                     \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06144                         prs[serie] = \textcolor{keyword}{new} Tuple<int, int>(prs[serie].Item1, rss.Count);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06145                     \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06146                     \textcolor{keywordflow}{for} (\textcolor{keywordtype}{int} r = prs[serie].Item1; r < prs[serie].Item2; r++)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06147                     \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06148                         b.Resolutions.Add(rss[r]);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06149                     \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06150                 \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06151                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06152                 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06153                     b.Resolutions.AddRange(rss);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06154                 \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06155             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06156             \textcolor{keywordflow}{else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06157                 b.Resolutions.AddRange(rss);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06158 }
\DoxyCodeLine{06159             \textcolor{comment}{//If we have 2 resolutions that we're not added they are the label \& macro resolutions so we add them to the image.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06160             \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (rss.Count -\/ pyramidResolutions == 2)}
\DoxyCodeLine{06161             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{06162                 b.Resolutions.Add(rss[rss.Count -\/ 2]);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06163                 b.Resolutions.Add(rss[rss.Count -\/ 1]);}
\DoxyCodeLine{06164             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{06165 }

{\em file} & The file parameter is a string that represents the file path or name where the data will be saved.\\

{\em id} & The \char`\"{}id\char`\"{} parameter is a string that represents an identifier for the save operation. It could be used to uniquely identify the saved data or to specify a specific location or format for the saved file.\\

{\em serie} & The \char`\"{}serie\char`\"{} parameter is an integer that represents a series or sequence number. It is used as a parameter in the Save\+Async method.\\
\hline
{\em ome} & The \char`\"{}ome\char`\"{} parameter is a boolean value that determines whether or not to perform a specific action in the saving process.\\

\index{BioImager.BioImage@{BioImager.BioImage}!SavePyramidalAsync@{SavePyramidalAsync}}
\index{SavePyramidalAsync@{SavePyramidalAsync}!BioImager.BioImage@{BioImager.BioImage}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{SavePyramidalAsync()}{SavePyramidalAsync()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily static async Task Bio\+Imager.\+Bio\+Image.\+Save\+Pyramidal\+Async (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}}\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{imgs,  }\item[{string}]{file,  }\item[{Enums.\+Foreign\+Tiff\+Compression}]{com,  }\item[{int}]{comp\+Level }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}



The function {\ttfamily Save\+Pyramidal\+Async} saves an array of {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}}} objects as a pyramidal TIFF file asynchronously.  


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em imgs} & imgs is an array of \mbox{\hyperlink{class_bio_imager_1_1_bio_image}{Bio\+Image}} objects.\\
\hline
{\em file} & The \char`\"{}file\char`\"{} parameter is a string that represents the file path where the pyramidal image will be saved.\\
\hline
{\em com} & The parameter \char`\"{}com\char`\"{} is of type Enums.\+Foreign\+Tiff\+Compression, which is an enumeration representing different compression options for the TIFF file.\\
\hline
{\em comp\+Level} & The {\ttfamily comp\+Level} parameter is an integer that represents the compression level for the TIFF file. It is used to specify the level of compression to be applied to the image data when saving the pyramidal image. The higher the compression level, the smaller the file size but potentially lower image quality.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The method is returning a boolean value. If the try block is executed successfully, it will return true. If an exception is caught, it will return false.
